  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_100d8b9b-a890-42d1-adbd-46d57aab6569'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer14533489500399182745">An allegorical fable of love, sacrifice and selfishness. As with all of Wilde's short stories it embodies strong moral values and is told with an effervescence akin to that of the 1001 nights. <br/><br/>It is the tale of a lovestruck student who must provide his lover with a red rose in order to win her heart. A nightingale overhearing his lament from a solitary oak tree is filled w</span>
  <span id="freeText14533489500399182745" style="display:none">An allegorical fable of love, sacrifice and selfishness. As with all of Wilde's short stories it embodies strong moral values and is told with an effervescence akin to that of the 1001 nights. <br /><br />It is the tale of a lovestruck student who must provide his lover with a red rose in order to win her heart. A nightingale overhearing his lament from a solitary oak tree is filled with sorrow and admiration all at once, and decides to help the poor young man.<br /><br />She journeys through the night seeking the perfect red rose and finally comes across a rambling rose bush but alas, the bush has no roses to offer her. However, there is a way to MAKE a red rose, but with grave consequences. <br /><br />This story can be found freely on many websites:<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.eastoftheweb.com/short-stories/UBooks/NigRos.shtml">http://www.eastoftheweb.com/short-sto...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.literaturepage.com/read/the-happy-prince-11.html">http://www.literaturepage.com/read/th...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.oscarwildecollection.com/">http://www.oscarwildecollection.com/</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14533489500399182745" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/899328-how-is-romantic-love-defeated-by">How is romantic love defeated by materialistic love in this story?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_899328'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F590272.The_Nightingale_and_the_Rose">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionTimestamp'>
<a href="/questions/899328-how-is-romantic-love-defeated-by">4 years ago</a>
</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/899328-how-is-romantic-love-defeated-by">Add your answer</a>
</li>
</ul>
</div>

</div>
<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/65201524-fioblustarz"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_100x100-6433b08cbe793211f55e184d39e84c4d.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/65201524-fioblustarz">FioBluStarz</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I dont think materialistic love defeated romantic love, the true love expressed in this story is neither the boy's love for the girl nor other way aro<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I dont think materialistic love defeated romantic love, the true love expressed in this story is neither the boy's love for the girl nor other way around. It is the nightingale's love for the love itself (which is represented as rose here) the highest form of love, as the nightingale was willing to entirely sacrifice itself for that love. Both the boy as well as the nightingale loved in this story. The nightingale's self-less love for love itself brought the rose to life. The boy's love which was blinded by intellect (also he was full of himself), brought back the same type of love towards him. That is one theory. Another one is, the nightingale's love for the boy was the purest, cuz you know it is pure love, when all you want is happiness for the one you love, even if you are not a part of that happiness. This is another theory. Either ways, the purest love wins. (aka the nightingale)<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>
</span>
</div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer295917027" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2218476798061409379">This is the saddest, most tragic story I've ever read. It starts out as a fairytale and you think it will end well. Love is described as the most beautiful thing in the world, by the nightingale outside the student's window.<br/><br/>“Be happy, cried the Nightingale, be happy; you shall have your red rose. I will build it out of music by moonlight, and stain it with my own heart's-blood. All that I ask of you in return is that you will be a true lover, for Love is wiser than Philosophy, though she is wise</span>
  <span id="freeText2218476798061409379" style="display:none">This is the saddest, most tragic story I've ever read. It starts out as a fairytale and you think it will end well. Love is described as the most beautiful thing in the world, by the nightingale outside the student's window.<br /><br />“Be happy, cried the Nightingale, be happy; you shall have your red rose. I will build it out of music by moonlight, and stain it with my own heart's-blood. All that I ask of you in return is that you will be a true lover, for Love is wiser than Philosophy, though she is wise, and mightier than Power, though he is mighty. Flame-coloured are his wings, and coloured like flame is his body. His lips are sweet as honey, and his breath is like frankincense.” <br /><br />But I should have seen it coming, the darkness. This is Oscar Wilde, after all. My heart burst and I felt pure pain for the nightingale's sacrifice. The picture that got stuck in my mind was the painfully colored rose lying in the gutter.<br /><br />Wilde is portraying people's idea of love as extremely shallow, while the nightingale serves as the only one with a true heart.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2218476798061409379" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_572128697" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/572128697" />
    <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani"><img alt="Ahmad Sharabiani" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1194930432p2/614778.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/572128697?book_show_action=true">Mar 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ahmad Sharabiani" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ahmad Sharabiani" href="/user/show/614778-ahmad-sharabiani">Ahmad Sharabiani</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer572128697" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8772349334327291692">The Nightingale and the Rose, Oscar Wilde <br/>A nightingale overhears a student complaining that his professor's daughter will not dance with him, as he is unable to give her a red rose. The nightingale visits all the rose-trees in the garden, and one of the white roses tell her that there's a way to produce a red rose, but only if the nightingale is prepared to sing the sweetest song for the rose all night, and sacrifice her life to do so. Seeing the student in tears, the nightingale carries out th</span>
  <span id="freeText8772349334327291692" style="display:none">The Nightingale and the Rose, Oscar Wilde <br />A nightingale overhears a student complaining that his professor's daughter will not dance with him, as he is unable to give her a red rose. The nightingale visits all the rose-trees in the garden, and one of the white roses tell her that there's a way to produce a red rose, but only if the nightingale is prepared to sing the sweetest song for the rose all night, and sacrifice her life to do so. Seeing the student in tears, the nightingale carries out the ritual, and impales herself on the rose-tree's thorn so that her heart's blood can stain the rose. The student takes the rose to the professor's daughter, but she again rejects him because another man has sent her some real jewels, and "everybody knows that jewels cost far more than flowers." The student angrily throws the rose into the gutter, returns to his study of metaphysics, and decides not to believe in true love anymore. Originally published: 1888.<br /><br />تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز چهارم ماه مارس سال 2005 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: داستانهای کوتاه اسکار وایلد؛ نویسنده: اسکار وایلد؛ مترجم: ماهرخ اشراقی؛ تهران، مشکی، 1384؛ در 154 ص؛ شابک: 9648765065؛<br /><br />فهرست داستانهای کوتاه اسکار وایلد: ماهیگیر جوان و روحش؛ غول خودخواه؛ شاهزاده ی خوشحال (خوشبخت)؛ بلبل و گل سرخ؛ فرزند ستاره<br /><br /><b>متن داستان: گل و بلبل</b><br /><br />دانشجوی جوان فریاد زد: او گفت اگر برایش گل سرخ ببرم با من میرقصد اما در سراسر باغم گل سرخی نیست بلبل از آشیانه اش در درخت شاه بلوط صدای او را شنید و از لابلای برگها فرونگریست و در شگفت شد<br /><br />دانشجو فریاد زد: در سرتاسر باغ من گل سرخی نیست! دریغ که خوشبختی به چه چیزهای کوچکی وابسته است! آنچه خردمندان نوشته اند مو به مو خوانده ام، و بر تمام رمزهای حکمت دست یافته ام – و با این همه تنها نیاز به یک گل سرخ، زندگیم را رو به شوربختی میبرد و چشمان زیبایش پر از اشک شد<br /><br />دانشجوی جوان زیر لب زمزمه کرد: فردا شب، شاهزاده مجلس رقصی دارد، و یار من در میان آن جمع است. اگر برایش گل سرخ ببرم – تا سپیده دم با من میرقصد. اگر برایش گل سرخ ببرم او را در آغوش خواهم گرفت، و او سر بر شانه ام خواهد نهاد و دستش با دستانم گره خواهد خورد. اما دریغ که در باغ من گل سرخ به هم نمیرسد! پس ناگزیر تنها خواهم نشست و او از کنارم خواهد گذشت – به من اعتنا نخواهد کرد و قلبم خواهد شکست<br /><br />بلبل گفت: به راستی عاشقی پاکباز است. او گرفتار همان دردی ست که من به نغمه میخوانم – آنچه مایه ی شادمانی من است – رنجورش میدارد! راستی که عشق چه شگفت انگیز است<br /><br />مارمولک سبز کوچکی که با دم علم کرده از کنارش میگذشت، پرسید: چرا گریه میکند؟<br />پروانه ای که سراسیمه در پی پرتوی از آفتاب، پر میزد، گفت: به راستی – چرا؟<br />گل مرواریدی با صدای نرم و نازک، در گوش همسایه اش نجوا کرد: به راستی – چرا؟<br /><br />بلبل گفت: به خاطر یک گل سرخ میگرید<br /><br />آنها فریاد زدند: برای یک گل سرخ؟ آه چه مسخره است! و مارمولک که از شمار عیب جویان بود، غش غش خندید<br /><br />اما بلبل راز پنهان غم دانشجو را دریافت، و خاموش بر درخت شاه بلوط نشست، و به رمز و راز عشق اندیشید. ناگاه بالهای قهوه ای رنگش را برای پرواز بگشود، و در دل آسمان اوج گرفت. همچون سایه از میان بیشه بگذشت، و سایه وار پهنای باغ را بپیمود. در میان چمنزار درخت گل سرخ زیبائی روئیده بود، و بلبل همین که آن را دید، راست به سویش پرکشید، و فریاد زد: یک گل سرخ به من بده من نیز برایت آواز میخوانم<br /><br />اما درخت گل، سرش را بالا برد، و پاسخ داد: گلهای من سفید است، سفیدتر از برف کوهسار، اما پیش برادرم برو که در پای ساعت قدیمی روئیده است و شاید آنچه را که میخواهی به تو بدهد<br /><br />از این رو بلبل به سوی درخت گلی که در پای ساعت آفتابی قدیمی روئیده بود، پر کشید. فریاد زد: یک گل سرخ به من بده و من شیرینترین آوازم را برایت میخوانم <br /><br />اما درخت گل سرش را بالا برد، و پاسخ داد: گل های من زرد است، به زردی گیسوان پری دریائی، که بر تخت عنبرین مینشیند. اما پیش برادرم برو که زیر پنجره ی دانشجو روئیده است، او شاید آنچه را که میخواهی به تو بدهد<br /><br />از اینرو بلبل به سوی درخت گلی که زیر پنجره دانشجو روئیده بود، پر کشید. فریاد زد: گل سرخی به من بده و من شیرینترین آوازم را برای تو میخوانم <br />اما درخت گل سرش را بالا برد، و پاسخ داد: گلهای من سرخ است، به سرخی پای کبوتران، و سرختر از خوشه های بزرگ مرجانها، که در غارهای دریا، پیوسته در پیچ و تاب هستند. اما زمستان نزدیک است، رگهایم از سرما فسرده، یخبندان جوانه هایم را خشکانده، و طوفان شاخه هایم بشکسته است، و امسال گل سرخی نخواهم داشت<br /><br />بلبل فریاد زد: تنها یک گل سرخ میخواهم، تنها یک گل سرخ! آیا راهی وجود ندارد که بتوانم گل سرخی پیدا کنم؟<br /><br />درخت پاسخ داد: تنها یک راه وجود دارد، اما چنان وحشت آور است که یارای گفتنش را ندارم<br /><br />بلبل گفت: بگو، نمیترسم<br /><br />درخت گفت: اگر گل سرخ میخواهی، باید آن را در مهتاب، از نغمه و نوا بسازی، و با خون دل خویش بدان رنگ دهی. باید سینه ات را بر خار بفشاری و برایم بخوانی. سراسر شب باید برایم بخوانی و خار بر قلبت بخلد، تا خونمایه ی زندگی ات در رگهایم روان شود و خون من گردد<br /><br />بلبل بانگ برداشت: مرگ بهای گزافی یرای یک شاخه گل سرخ است، و زندگی برای همه عزیز است. نشستن در جنگل سرسبز و خورشید را در ارابه ی طلاییش، و ماه را در ارابه ی مرواریدش نگریستن، بسیار دلنواز است. اما باز عشق از زندگی برتر است، و قلب پرنده در برابر قلب انسان چه وزنی دارد؟<br /><br />پس بالهای قهوه ای رنگش را باز کرد، و در دل آسمان اوج گرفت. شتابان از فراز باغ گذشت و سایه وار در میان بیشه زار پر زد<br /><br />دانشجو در همانجا که بلبل او را دیده بود و از کنارش رفته بود، روی چمنزار دراز کشیده بود، و اشک چشمانش، هنوز نخشکیده بود<br /><br />بلبل بانگ زد: شاد باش، شاد باش! گل سرخ را خواهی یافت. آن را در روشنائی مهتاب از نغمه و نوا میسازم، و با خون دل خود بدان رنگ میدهم، اما در برابر آن تنها خواهشی از تو دارم، و آن این است که عاشقی پاکباز باشی <br /><br />دانشجو از روی چمن فرانگریست و گوش داد، اما از گفته های بلبل هیچ درنیافت <br /><br />اما درخت شاه بلوط فهمید، و اندوهگین شد، زیرا به بلبل کوچک که بر شاخه هایش آشیانه ساخته بود، مهر میورزید <br /><br />درخت زمزمه کرد: واپسین سرودت را برای من بخوان. وقتی تو بروی، من سخت تنها خواهم ماند! بدینسان بلبل برای درخت شاه بلوط آواز خواند، و صدایش بسان صدای ریزش آب از تنگ نقره بود<br /><br />هنگامی که ماه در آسمان درخشیدن گرفت، بلبل به سوی درخت گل سرخ پر کشید، و نشست و سینه اش را بر خار فشرد. سراسر شب خواند و خواند و سینه اش بر خار بود. و خار هر لحظه بیشتر در سینه اش میخلید، و خونمایه هستی اش از او بیرون میتراوید. نخست از پیدایش عشق در دل یک پسر و دختر خواند، تا بر بلندترین شاخه درخت، گل سرخی دلفریب شکفت، هر نغمه ای که در پی نغمه ای برمیآمد، گلبرگی بر گلبرگهای دیگر میافزود. گلبرگ نخست بیرنگ بود، همچون مه ای شناور بر فراز رودخانه، همچون پای بامدادان، بی رنگ. اما درخت بر بلبل بانگ زد، تا سینه اش را هرچه بیشتر بر خار بفشرد <br /><br />درخت فریاد زد: بلبل کوچک! بیشتر بفشار، و گرنه پیش از آنکه گل سرخ را تمام کنی، روز درمیرسد<br /><br />از این رو بلبل خود را بیشتر بر خار فشرد و آوازش پیوسته بلندتر شد، زیرا از پیدایش اشتیاق در جان یک مرد و زن میخواند. بدین گونه بلبل خود را بازهم بیشتر بر خار فشرد، و خار به قلب او رسید، و دردی جانکاه بر جانش چنگ زد، و در سراسر تنش دوید. درد هر دم جانکاهتر میشد، و آوازش هرچه عنان گسیخته تر، زیرا از عشقی میسرود که با مرگ کامل میشود، عشقی که در گور هم نمیمیرد <br /><br />صدای بلبل هر دم ناتوانتر گردید، و بالهای کوچکش لرزیدن گرفت. آوازش هر دم ضعیفتر شد، و ناگهان حس کرد چیزی سخت، راه گلویش را میبندد. آنگاه واپسین نوایش را از حنجره برآورد <br /><br />ماه سپید، آن را شنید، و دمیدن سپیده را از یاد برد، و در آسمان درنگ ورزید<br /><br />گل سرخ آن را شنید و سراپایش با شوق و شادی لرزید، و گلبرگهایش را از خواب ناز برانگیخت <br /><br />درخت فریاد زد: نگاه کن! نگاه کن! گل سرخ کامل شده <br /><br />اما بلبل پاسخ نداد، چه، مرده در میان سبزه های بلند افتاده بود، و خاری در دل داشت<br /><br />باری ظهر هنگام، دانشجو پنجره ی اتاقش را بگشود، و به بیرون نگاه کرد، و فریاد زد: آه خدایا! چه بخت بلندی گل سرخی در اینجا شکفته است! در تمام عمرم گل سرخی به این زیبائی ندیده ام. چه زیباست. آنگاه کلاهش را بر سر نهاد، و گل سرخ به دست به خانه ی استاد رفت <br /><br />دختر استاد بر آستانه ی در نشسته بود، دانشجو با صدای بلند گفت: گفتی اگر برایت گل سرخ بیاورم با من خواهی رقصید، اینهم سرخترین گل جهان! امشب آنرا بر سینه ات، کنار قلب خود بیاویز، و هنگامی که با هم میرقصیم، به تو خواهم گفت که چقدر دوستت دارم <br /><br />اما دختر رو درهم کشید، و پاسخ داد: گمان نمیکنم به لباسهایم بیاید، و از این گذشته پسر برادر پیشکار، برایم چند جواهر اصل فرستاده، و پیداست که ارزش جواهر بسیار بیش از گل است <br /><br />دانشجو با خشم و برافروختگی گفت: باشد، اما به شرفم قسم که تو بسیار ناسپاسی، و گل سرخ را به خیابان افکند، و گل یکراست در میان لای و لجن افتاد، و درشکه ای از روی آن گذشت<br />پایان؛ <br /><br />به گفتاری از «اسکار وایلد»: ایشان این داستان را، پس از خوانش غزل «بلبلی برگ گلی خوشرنگ در منقار داشت - وندر آن برگ و نوا خوش ناله های زار داشت. گفتمش در عین وصل این ناله و فریاد چیست؛ - گفت ما را جلوه ی معشوق بر اینکار داشت.» از حافظ شیرازی، بنوشته اند. ا. شربیانی</span>
  <a data-text-id="8772349334327291692" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer6724170322969509710">A handsome young student is having what we would nowadays term a 'hissy fit' because there isn't a single red rose in his entire garden; he desperately needs some to present to his crush.<br/>"For want of a red rose is my life made wretched?" he wails.<br/>A nightingale watches from above, heartened that it has at last witnessed a true lover.   <span id="freeText6724170322969509710" style="display:none">A handsome young student is having what we would nowadays term a 'hissy fit' because there isn't a single red rose in his entire garden; he desperately needs some to present to his crush.<br />"For want of a red rose is my life made wretched?" he wails.<br />A nightingale watches from above, heartened that it has at last witnessed a true lover. The bird represents one of the few romantics in this cynical world - unlike the lizard, the butterfly and even the whispering daisies - who all think that the young human is simply getting himself upset over nothing. <br /><br />Oscar Wilde, channelling his own romantic battles in the face of hostility, brings us a beautiful little fairytale with themes focussing on the extreme sacrifices we make to find true love - but also on the selfishness of those who don't deserve it. <br /><br />Wonderful use of anthropomorphism too. <br />Well done Oscar!<br /><br />Free to read online: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://hs.kku.ac.th/ichuso/2018/ICHUSO-078.pdf">https://hs.kku.ac.th/ichuso/2018/ICHU...</a></span>

<div id="review_1859540888" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1859540888" />
    <a title="Sarah" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49360584-sarah"><img alt="Sarah" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580400925p2/49360584.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1859540888?book_show_action=true">Jan 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah" href="/user/show/49360584-sarah">Sarah</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49360584-sarah?shelf=2017-reads">2017-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49360584-sarah?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49360584-sarah?shelf=short-stories">short-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer1859540888&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1859540888" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17524444539687732230">The Nightingale and The Rose is a heartbreaking story about the nature of love and sacrifice. At the beginning of the story, we are given the impression that the love between the student and the girl is a true love. Later, we are struck with the truth. Their love turns out to be a shallow one based on materialistic happiness. At the end the student gives up on his love because it was not true in the first place.<br/><br/> <b>“What a silly thing Love is. It is not as useful as Logic, for it does not prove any</b></span>
  <span id="freeText17524444539687732230" style="display:none">The Nightingale and The Rose is a heartbreaking story about the nature of love and sacrifice. At the beginning of the story, we are given the impression that the love between the student and the girl is a true love. Later, we are struck with the truth. Their love turns out to be a shallow one based on materialistic happiness. At the end the student gives up on his love because it was not true in the first place.<br /><br /> <b>“What a silly thing Love is. It is not as useful as Logic, for it does not prove anything, and it is always telling one of things that are not going to happen, and making one believe things that are not true. In fact, it is quite unpractical, and, as in this age to be practical is everything, I shall go back to Philosophy and study Metaphysics.” </b> <br /><br />And we are left to ponder the nightingale’s sacrifice; was it worth it? Or was it all in vain? The nightingale believed it was worthwhile. For him, it mattered immensely. But does it really matter??<br /><br /><b>“Death is a great price to pay for a red rose,” cried the Nightingale, “and Life is very dear to all .....Yet Love is better than Life, and what is the heart of a bird compared to the heart of a man?” </b><br /><br />A great read. Highly recommended.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17524444539687732230" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

I melted. I remembered the times before reality, cynicism and societal manliness invaded my romantic, child-like heart. My eyes burned with the production of moistness.<br /><br />I opened to Oscar. He said, "Relax. Trust me. Look deep inside. Remember. Don't be afraid of the ideologies of love you once knew. I'm trying to tell you something." I loosened. My eyes fixed in a trance. He made me mad. Shocked me. Why would someone do this? Why mock such a loving sacrifice? I looked up meanings and understand. <br /><br />Lust, selfishness, greed counterfeit true love. They crush it underfoot, the true tragedy of humanity.<br /><br />But I'm still like, "What the hell man!"</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2228970705?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laysee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laysee" href="/user/show/4863523-laysee">Laysee</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2228970705" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9231846118221287503">“...life is very dear to all. It is pleasant to sit in the green wood, and to watch the sun in his chariot of gold, and the moon in her chariot of pearl...Yet love is better than life and what is the heart of a bird compared to the heart of a man?” - Oscar Wilde<br/><br/><b>The Nightingale and The Rose</b> by Oscar Wilde is a satirical and heart-breaking story about love - the all-consuming passion of which nightingales sing and the self-serving quest of the heart that some humans choose to make of it. <br/><br/>A nightin</span>
  <span id="freeText9231846118221287503" style="display:none">“...life is very dear to all. It is pleasant to sit in the green wood, and to watch the sun in his chariot of gold, and the moon in her chariot of pearl...Yet love is better than life and what is the heart of a bird compared to the heart of a man?” - Oscar Wilde<br /><br /><b>The Nightingale and The Rose</b> by Oscar Wilde is a satirical and heart-breaking story about love - the all-consuming passion of which nightingales sing and the self-serving quest of the heart that some humans choose to make of it. <br /><br />A nightingale in a holm-oak tree heard a young student weeping because he did not have a red rose. His love interest said she would dance with him only if he brought her one. He wept for opportunities he knew he would never have. “Ah, on what little things does happiness depend.” <br /><br />The nightingale who sang of love understood its mystery, and was deeply affected. She flew to every rose bush in the garden and asked to sing her sweetest song for a red rose. But it would take much more than a song to procure a fiery red rose in the heart of winter. The nightingale who believed in true love was willing to make the supreme sacrifice. <br /><br />Love, after all, is a lavish emotion. If only the young man and the girl of his dreams understood love the way the nightingale did. What a travesty! In this instance, the heart of a man cannot hold a candle to the heart of a bird. And my heart ached for the nightingale.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9231846118221287503" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1917446163" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1917446163" />
    <a title="Mohsin Maqbool" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3332742-mohsin-maqbool"><img alt="Mohsin Maqbool" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1373637583p2/3332742.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1917446163?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mohsin Maqbool" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mohsin Maqbool" href="/user/show/3332742-mohsin-maqbool">Mohsin Maqbool</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1917446163" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10405463369067625739"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487461459i/22016327._SX540_.jpg' width='500' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><b>A magnificent illustration of "The Nightingale and the Rose" by Del Kathryn Barton and Brendan Fletcher.</b><br/> <br/>OSCAR Fingal O'Flahertie Wills Wilde (October 16, 1854 – November 30, 1900) was an Irish playwright, novelist, poet, and short story writer. He was known for his barbed wit and was one of the most successful playwrights of late Victorian London.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487461459i/22016328.jpg' width='355' height='504' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><b>A poster for the stage production of "The Nightingale and the Rose" at the Bristol Museum in February 2014.</b><br/><br/> Wilde’s “The Nightingale and the Rose” i</span>
  <span id="freeText10405463369067625739" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487461459i/22016327._SX540_.jpg" width="500" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><b>A magnificent illustration of "The Nightingale and the Rose" by Del Kathryn Barton and Brendan Fletcher.</b><br> <br>OSCAR Fingal O'Flahertie Wills Wilde (October 16, 1854 – November 30, 1900) was an Irish playwright, novelist, poet, and short story writer. He was known for his barbed wit and was one of the most successful playwrights of late Victorian London.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487461459i/22016328.jpg" width="355" height="504" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><b>A poster for the stage production of "The Nightingale and the Rose" at the Bristol Museum in February 2014.</b><br><br> Wilde’s “The Nightingale and the Rose” is a short story full of irony. It tells about a student who falls in love with a young woman. However, the latter demands that he gift her with a red rose if he truly loves her. The youth goes about looking for a red rose in the garden but in vain. Filled with moroseness, he starts crying. <br> A nightingale perched on the branch of a tree is watching all this. She utters, “Surely Love is a wonderful thing. It is more precious than emeralds, and dearer than fine opals. Pearls and pomegranates cannot buy it, nor is it set forth in the marketplace. It may not be purchased of the merchants, nor can it be weighed out in the balance for gold."<br> She decides to get a red rose for the student so that he can attain his love. She goes to a rose tree and asks it for a red rose. <br> "If you want a red rose," said the Tree, "you must build it out of music by moonlight, and stain it with your own heart's blood. You must sing to me with your breast against a thorn. All night long you must sing to me, and the thorn must pierce your heart, and your life-blood must flow into my veins, and become mine."<br> "Death is a great price to pay for a red rose," cried the Nightingale, "and Life is very dear to all. It is pleasant to sit in the green wood, and to watch the Sun in his chariot of gold, and the Moon in her chariot of pearl. Sweet is the scent of the hawthorn, and sweet are the bluebells that hide in the valley, and the heather that blows on the hill. Yet Love is better than Life, and what is the heart of a bird compared to the heart of a man?"<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487462556i/22016457._SY540_.jpg" width="200" height="320" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><b>"The Nightingale and the Rose" on an iPhon.</b><br><br> The Nightingale has the strongest character in the story. The Nightingale is willing to give up her life just so that the student can get a rose for his Lady Love. She proves that she has a heart of gold and is willing to sacrifice herself to help a human being. She proves herself to be more humane than a human can ever be.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487465538i/22016680._SX540_.jpg" width="450" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><b>A beautiful book cover of Wilde's moving short story.</b><br><br> The young woman has the most negative character in the story. She is greedy and selfish and seems only hungry for worldly desires. First she wants a red rose and when she gets it, she does not seem to care for it anymore and wants jewels instead. In fact, another youth has already promised it to her. The student’s character too is not flawless. When the Nightingale tells him, “Be happy; you shall have your red rose. I will build it out of music by moonlight, and stain it with my own heart's-blood. All that I ask of you in return is that you will be a true lover, for Love is wiser than philosophy,” he seems to be immune to her feelings. He studies Philosophy, yet he can’t understand these simple words from a bird who is going to sacrifice her life so that his desire gets fulfilled. Even the Oak-tree is more sensible as she understands and feels sorry for the bird as it knows what is going to happen to her in the end. The Nightingale’s future is certainly not rosy. It can only see the world through rose-tinted glasses!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487462556i/22016458._SX540_.jpg" width="520" height="249" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>My Love resides in my heart and within my eye.</b><br> <br> Wilde also seems to be mocking Victorian society which seems to measure love with materialism. True love can never be measured and is worth more in weight than all the diamonds, pearls, gold and silver on earth put together.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487461459i/22016331.jpg" width="500" height="424" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><b>The picture speaks for itself.</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="10405463369067625739" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1651203820" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1651203820" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5512657-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1543780395p2/5512657.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1651203820?book_show_action=true">May 10, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/5512657-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780195202311" href="/book/show/388469.The_Nightingale_and_the_Rose">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=short-stories-novellas">short-stories-novellas</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5512657-sara?shelf=breakfast-club">breakfast-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1651203820" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3914400670442933085">If anyone knew the risks of loving, it was no doubt Oscar Wilde. He served time in prison for his love,<br/> and his time in prison precipitated his death. The Nightingale and the Rose is one of his fairy tales, of which he wrote a collection. <br/><br/>A story about love and sacrifice and the risk that that sacrifice will be undeserved and unappreciated. The only one in this story who understands love is the nightingale. The bird says, "Yet Love is better than Life, and what is the heart of a bird compared to</span>
  <span id="freeText3914400670442933085" style="display:none">If anyone knew the risks of loving, it was no doubt Oscar Wilde. He served time in prison for his love,<br /> and his time in prison precipitated his death. The Nightingale and the Rose is one of his fairy tales, of which he wrote a collection. <br /><br />A story about love and sacrifice and the risk that that sacrifice will be undeserved and unappreciated. The only one in this story who understands love is the nightingale. The bird says, "Yet Love is better than Life, and what is the heart of a bird compared to the heart of a man?” In this case, the heart of the bird is much purer than the heart of the man. When she sings to him of her coming sacrifice, the student cannot understand her at all, which may well be a metaphor for how little man understands of love.<br /><br />In the end, love, in the form of the rose, is tossed away and the Nightingale has sacrificed herself in vain. She has failed to recognize that the student's love is not real or meaningful, but that does not lessen the fact that her love is both of those things. Her sacrifice is real, even if it is made for an undeserving cause, and it is not diminished by the callous use the rose comes to. Perhaps one of the themes here is that love never diminishes the true lover, even if the object of that feeling is wholly undeserving.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3914400670442933085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1487143457" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1487143457" />
    <a title="Sumati" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13187326-sumati"><img alt="Sumati" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1547181950p2/13187326.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1487143457?book_show_action=true">Dec 31, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sumati" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sumati" href="/user/show/13187326-sumati">Sumati</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/24268531-the-nightingale-and-the-rose-original-1888-edition">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13187326-sumati?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1487143457" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14221811400545078932">This story should be said orally or even better if presented as a musical. I really liked the way this story was told. A young lad, deeply in love with a girl who promised him a dance only if he brought a red rose for her, is in agony over not having a rose for his love. This agonizing was heard by a Nightingale who then flew around from tree to tree to find a red rose for the boy’s ‘true love’. She did find a rose but had to sacrifice her the blood from her heart to color it red. Her blood, her</span>
  <span id="freeText14221811400545078932" style="display:none">This story should be said orally or even better if presented as a musical. I really liked the way this story was told. A young lad, deeply in love with a girl who promised him a dance only if he brought a red rose for her, is in agony over not having a rose for his love. This agonizing was heard by a Nightingale who then flew around from tree to tree to find a red rose for the boy’s ‘true love’. She did find a rose but had to sacrifice her the blood from her heart to color it red. Her blood, her painful song, her falling pulse, her failing heart bloomed the rose into life but Alas! her sacrifice found no true love. It was only crushed under a cart. The girl didn’t want it nor did the boy. <br /><br />The Nightingale and the Rose is an allegory of selflessness and selfishness often claimed as Wilde’s own agony and battle to find a place for his own feelings in this society. The nightingale’s sacrificial nature is much reflective of Wilde himself during his end years when he sacrificed his freedom for the love of his male lover. Well, the nightingale did all in vain much like Wilde who also did it, maybe all in vain. Life still moved on even after he accepted his sexuality in the society. All that he got was a spiteful crowd laughing at his misery. <br /><br />This story stands true for any common man. There are people, who sacrifice their life and suffer to help someone, but at the end they aren’t returned with the same emotional intensity; possible, their actions were never even comprehended. In an age and period when most people appear to be interested only in their own welfare, without being able to look beyond their limited, subjective perspective, thus failing to see what or who is outside the borders of their very narrow egoistic world.<br /><br />PS: <b>Promod Nair</b>: My Friend, I found roses and love again here but, this time, I know why &amp; how they both are related. Thank you again for the review of <i>'Poetry of Roses'</i>. I have shared the link of your review below. :). Thanks again.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1434632878?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="14221811400545078932" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2387463485" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11632029236396336950">3★<br/>This is a little fable, parable, fairytale, what-have-you written by a man who's famous for his wit and wild ways. The writer often quoted as saying: <b>"I never travel without my diary. One should always have something sensational to read in the train."</b><br/><br/>This little story is not that. It's a very short love story where a young student pines for a girl who has said she will dance with him if he gives her a red rose. He dreams that if he dances with her, she will fall in love with him and so on unti</span>
  <span id="freeText11632029236396336950" style="display:none">3★<br />This is a little fable, parable, fairytale, what-have-you written by a man who's famous for his wit and wild ways. The writer often quoted as saying: <b>"I never travel without my diary. One should always have something sensational to read in the train."</b><br /><br />This little story is not that. It's a very short love story where a young student pines for a girl who has said she will dance with him if he gives her a red rose. He dreams that if he dances with her, she will fall in love with him and so on until happily ever after.<br /><br /><b>"<i>'No red rose in all my garden!'</i> he cried, and his beautiful eyes filled with tears. <i>'Ah, on what little things does happiness depend! I have read all that the wise men have written, and all the secrets of philosophy are mine, yet for want of a red rose is my life made wretched.'</i></b><br /><br />As he frets and worries about where he will ever find a red rose, a nightingale overhears him and decides to intervene. I will leave it there. I understand it as advising us to be careful what we wish for and to open our eyes to what we have. He obviously didn't really absorb all those secrets of philosophy.<br /><br />It's not going to entertain you for long on the train, I'm afraid.<br /><br />It's an odd little tale, one that was suggested by the Reading for Pleasure Group Breakfast Club.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/19267025-breakfast-club-buddy-reads-for-april---june-2018">https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/...</a><br /><br />You can find the free online here. <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.eastoftheweb.com/short-stories/UBooks/NigRos.shtml#3">http://www.eastoftheweb.com/short-sto...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="11632029236396336950" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2387875252" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17936783294189067586">I read this short story because it was recommended by a friend and because it still amazes me how few works I read by Oscar Wilde. <br/><br/>'The Nightingale and the Rose' is a fable that comes with a very clear and strong message. I actually read the story once before but wasn't aware of the fact that it is written by Wilde. However, I noticed the familiarity almost right away although it has been years which means the story stayed with me. <br/>I also like the way it was written and believe the prose suits t</span>
  <span id="freeText17936783294189067586" style="display:none">I read this short story because it was recommended by a friend and because it still amazes me how few works I read by Oscar Wilde. <br /><br />'The Nightingale and the Rose' is a fable that comes with a very clear and strong message. I actually read the story once before but wasn't aware of the fact that it is written by Wilde. However, I noticed the familiarity almost right away although it has been years which means the story stayed with me. <br />I also like the way it was written and believe the prose suits the topic as well as the message. At least the message that I understood - there might be more ways to interpret the fable. It is a bitter-sweet tale that just holds enough melancholia to make me emotional for a while. <br /><br />Since it's such a short work I won't tell much about its content. You can find it here for free: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.eastoftheweb.com/short-stories/UBooks/NigRos.shtml">http://www.eastoftheweb.com/short-sto...</a><br /><br />I'm glad that I reread the story - it actually made me wonder if I should give short stories another go. I forced myself to read them in the past which might not have been the best way. I was convinced that short stories just don't work for me because I always want more. I'm prepared to change my opinion. Is anyone willing to point me in the direction of their favorite short story? </span>
  <a data-text-id="17936783294189067586" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('3ho0k5E9t5QljVz9kDGCWbVZOK0GfgfW0rRSlg6x8zF0gaDKNfz6+5TJ0kXy8E2bSCLL2IrSwyldKlDPuyWZdQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JjX/LCuxRmgFBqKAslEPMYR0WpGEm03QgYK+zXJHD7KMrmt1j3ALB7RCLDjQkMDzeQ+p5Ag3iS8OHLyUx9Nl9g==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15836526853256644485">Oscar Fingal O'Flahertie Wills Wilde was an Irish playwright, poet, and author of numerous short stories, and one novel. Known for his biting wit, and a plentitude of aphorisms, he became one of the most successful playwrights of the late Victorian era in London, and one of the greatest celebrities of his day. Several of his plays continue to be widely performed, especially <i>The Importance of Being</i></span>
  <span id="freeText15836526853256644485" style="display:none">Oscar Fingal O'Flahertie Wills Wilde was an Irish playwright, poet, and author of numerous short stories, and one novel. Known for his biting wit, and a plentitude of aphorisms, he became one of the most successful playwrights of the late Victorian era in London, and one of the greatest celebrities of his day. Several of his plays continue to be widely performed, especially <i>The Importance of Being Earnest</i>. <br /><br />As the result of a widely covered series of trials, Wilde suffered a dramatic downfall and was imprisoned for two years hard labour after being convicted of "gross indecency" with other men. After Wilde was released from prison he set sail for Dieppe by the night ferry. He never returned to Ireland or Britain, and died in poverty.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15836526853256644485" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
